  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_f927f06b-8432-466a-a27d-e813669cac86'
      });

  <span id="freeText4805331023876730515" style="display:none">Author Patricia Reilly Giff's Newbery Honor-winning Lily's Crossing is now available for the first time in paperback!<br /><br />Every summer Lily and her father go to her family's house in Rockaway, near the Atlantic Ocean. But the summer of 1944 is different. World War II has called Lily's father overseas, Lily's best friend Margaret had to move with her family to a wartime factory town, and Lily is forced to live with her grandmother. But then a boy named Albert, a refugee from Hungary, comes to live in Rockaway. He has lost most of his family to the war. Soon he and Lily form a special friendship, and they have secrets to share. But they have both told lies, and Lily's lie may cost Albert his life.</span>

<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">I agree with the previous comments that this book is perfect for an 11 year old with enjoys historical fiction like Number the Stars. The story itself<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">I agree with the previous comments that this book is perfect for an 11 year old with enjoys historical fiction like Number the Stars. The story itself is told from the point of view of an 11 year old girl, so it would be relatable in terms of age. <br /><br />From a teacher's perspective, this book is age and reading level appropriate.<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1729733559?book_show_action=true">Aug 15, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13244359-donna?shelf=youth-young-adult-fiction">youth-young-adult-fiction</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1729733559" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17400191158407721556">This book is a children's book that won a Newbery Honor in 1998. It is set during WWII as a little girl's father goes off to war and she is living with her grandmother. She is a bit of a brat, but I like the way the author opens her up and makes it so that she can be understood, even in her naughty ways. As hard as she thinks she has it, she meets someone who has it even harder. <br/><br/>I'm clearly not the target audience for this book, but I like that there are books like these that can get kids to won</span>
  <span id="freeText17400191158407721556" style="display:none">This book is a children's book that won a Newbery Honor in 1998. It is set during WWII as a little girl's father goes off to war and she is living with her grandmother. She is a bit of a brat, but I like the way the author opens her up and makes it so that she can be understood, even in her naughty ways. As hard as she thinks she has it, she meets someone who has it even harder. <br /><br />I'm clearly not the target audience for this book, but I like that there are books like these that can get kids to wonder.</span>

          </span>

<div id="review_305594654" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/305594654" />
    <a title="Corena Fitch" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7606846-corena-fitch"><img alt="Corena Fitch" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/305594654?book_show_action=true">Apr 02, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Corena Fitch" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Corena Fitch" href="/user/show/7606846-corena-fitch">Corena Fitch</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer305594654" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16746342255475624444">Lily’s Crossing is a historical fiction book that takes place in the summer of 1944, during World War II. Lily is a young girl who is about to start her summer in Rockaway Beach with her grandmother. She has plans to fish and spend time with her good friend Margret who lives there. Her father is supposed to visit every weekend and share in her time there. Nothing goes as it is planned though; Margret’s family has to move because her father must start making bomber planes for the war and Lily’s f</span>
  <span id="freeText16746342255475624444" style="display:none">Lily’s Crossing is a historical fiction book that takes place in the summer of 1944, during World War II. Lily is a young girl who is about to start her summer in Rockaway Beach with her grandmother. She has plans to fish and spend time with her good friend Margret who lives there. Her father is supposed to visit every weekend and share in her time there. Nothing goes as it is planned though; Margret’s family has to move because her father must start making bomber planes for the war and Lily’s father’s first weekend visit comes with terrible news. He must go overseas and help the allied troops. Lily is devastated. Even though her summer and life seems to have fallen apart, she meets a young boy named Albert who has been affected by the war also. Together they find strength each other’s friendship and become best friends sharing emotional experiences that will last a lifetime.<br />I would recommend this book be read as it is a great way for us to get a feel for the fears of this time period. There are many references to planes flying overhead and you could feel the fear of the characters wondering if it was a Nazi plane. While some feel the separation of loved ones from wars today, it shows how it was different then. You would not even know where loved ones were for weeks if you were lucky. There was no internet, no Skype, and no communication except for an occasional letter. This book because of the reading level and subject matter would be good for advanced ages (12-18).<br />This book had no illustrations. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="16746342255475624444" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer755873903186409707">Lily loves to lie. The lies flow fast and easy. Each time she vows not to lie, another one slides right on out of her mouth. Lily just cannot help herself.<br/><br/>The setting is Rockaway, NJ where Lily, her grandmother and father spend idyllic summers. But the summer of 1944 is different and lives are changed because of WWII. Lily's best friend moves to Detroit where her father can build bombs, the seaside boardwalk is empty and Lily's father is going oversees to fight in the war.<br/><br/>Having lost a mother in</span>
  <span id="freeText755873903186409707" style="display:none">Lily loves to lie. The lies flow fast and easy. Each time she vows not to lie, another one slides right on out of her mouth. Lily just cannot help herself.<br /><br />The setting is Rockaway, NJ where Lily, her grandmother and father spend idyllic summers. But the summer of 1944 is different and lives are changed because of WWII. Lily's best friend moves to Detroit where her father can build bombs, the seaside boardwalk is empty and Lily's father is going oversees to fight in the war.<br /><br />Having lost a mother in childhood, Lily knows the fear of abandonment and loneliness. When a young Hungarian refugee arrives, Lily learns the unspeakable things Albert experienced in losing his family during Nazi occupation.<br /><br />Slipping into her habit of pathological lying seems harmless until one places Albert's life in jeopardy.<br /><br />This 1998 Newbery Honor book is highly recommended. The themes of loss, grief, friendship, the impact of war and the repercussions of actions are all packed into a mere 180 pages. ( )</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer66962384" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17637737554656058460">I saw this at the library--it's a Newbery awarded book so I thought I would read it. This book was set near the end of WWII and offers a different perspective of the war than I had previously read. It's an easy summer read and I think for kids, a good eye-opener to some of the hard things kids had to go through during the war.<br/><br/>What I didn't like: The protagonist is naughty, she steals, lies, sneaks into movies, and is mean to her grandmother. The whole first half of the book all I could think was</span>
  <span id="freeText17637737554656058460" style="display:none">I saw this at the library--it's a Newbery awarded book so I thought I would read it. This book was set near the end of WWII and offers a different perspective of the war than I had previously read. It's an easy summer read and I think for kids, a good eye-opener to some of the hard things kids had to go through during the war.<br /><br />What I didn't like: The protagonist is naughty, she steals, lies, sneaks into movies, and is mean to her grandmother. The whole first half of the book all I could think was I hope my kids don't act like this when they are 11 (or read this book and get ideas). It was distracting for sure. In the end she learned from her behavior, but I'm not sure, aside from some of her misdeeds that directed the storyline, the message was clear to not do those things. It's funny how your perspective changes after becoming a parent!</span>
  <a data-text-id="17637737554656058460" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer8102572630949057895">Lily is a child living in Rockaway, NY in 1944. The war has destroyed all her summer plans. Her best friend has left with her parents to go to Detroit. Lily's father is sent to the war front. What does Lily have left to make her summer memorable? Then a boy refugee from Hungary arrives and becomes her friend.   <span id="freeText8102572630949057895" style="display:none">Lily is a child living in Rockaway, NY in 1944. The war has destroyed all her summer plans. Her best friend has left with her parents to go to Detroit. Lily's father is sent to the war front. What does Lily have left to make her summer memorable? Then a boy refugee from Hungary arrives and becomes her friend. Both children have secrets that might tear their relationship apart. Lily's secret is that she tells tall tales quite often and something she said might injure or kill her new friend. <br /><br />I think the author does a great job creating the gloomy mood of New Yorkers as the war continues. The futile attempts to learn to swim mirror my experiences. However, the fact that the boy from Hungary speaks great English was totally unrealistic.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer9223017869686315659"><br/><br/>LILY’S CROSSING ⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️ I read this middle grade book as part of my personal challenge to read books recommended by my family. My sister read LILY’S CROSSING in elementary school and asked me to read this milestone, childhood book. I loved the different layers of the story. Lily is an American girl living out adventures on her summer vacation during WW2. So much of her world comes undone, but Lily’s spirit, hopefulness, and spunkiness prevail.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer15457907582234640237">Having read a number of children's books about WWII written in the 1940s and 1950s, I felt that the writing style of this book just didn't work. It has a modern feel that doesn't fit well, and the references to music, etc. seem contrived and researched (even though the author was born in 1935 and lived through the period). </span>

          </span>

<div id="review_3303520060" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3303520060" />
    <a title="Rachel Brown" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/109932600-rachel-brown"><img alt="Rachel Brown" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3303520060?book_show_action=true">Apr 26, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rachel Brown" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rachel Brown" href="/user/show/109932600-rachel-brown">Rachel Brown</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3303520060" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13696780618411097936">As World War II rages on in the summer of 1944, young Lily Mollahan finds herself in Rockaway, New York, enjoying her summer missing her father Poppy, who was called out to help build U.S. war ships, and her best friend Margaret, whose father was called out to build U.S. aircrafts in Detroit. Lily has a bad habit of lying to those around her. When she meets and befriends Hungarian refugee Albert, will another lie Lily weaves cost the friends their lives?<br/><br/>Terrel A. Young, one of the authors of Chi</span>
  <span id="freeText13696780618411097936" style="display:none">As World War II rages on in the summer of 1944, young Lily Mollahan finds herself in Rockaway, New York, enjoying her summer missing her father Poppy, who was called out to help build U.S. war ships, and her best friend Margaret, whose father was called out to build U.S. aircrafts in Detroit. Lily has a bad habit of lying to those around her. When she meets and befriends Hungarian refugee Albert, will another lie Lily weaves cost the friends their lives?<br /><br />Terrel A. Young, one of the authors of Children’s Literature, Briefly, state “if a book is truly well written, the words between its cover are arranged in almost magical patterns that stir deep emotional responses in readers,” (Young, 27). That being said, I do think Lily’s Crossing is a quality historical fiction. Plot, characters, setting, style and language, and theme are factors that are evaluated in fiction books to determine if they are of quality. The plot of Lily’s Crossing is very believable; a little girl struggling with her new-found life with the absence of her father and best friend and how to navigate her summer without them. With the chapters often ending on a cliff-hanger, Lily’s Crossing definitely made me want to keep reading to find out what happens next. The characters in Lily’s Crossing are believable and the protagonist Lily is dynamic. The friendship between Lily and Albert is sweet and innocent; something you would find in a real friendship between young children. The internal shift Lily experiences about her constant lying makes her a very dynamic character. <br /><br />The setting in Lily’s Crossing is believable and is integral to the story. Wartime during the 1940s is a common memory for those who lived through it, such as my own Grandmothers'. If Lily’s Crossing was set in the Midwest for example, Lily would not have been able to see the huge warships sailing on the Atlantic Ocean or hear the constant roar of aircrafts overhead. The style and language used in Lily’s Crossing does stir emotions. Because Lily’s Crossing is narrated through an omniscient narrator, the reader is able to know what Lily is doing and thinking, as well as what is occurring in the setting. The theme of friendship in Lily’s Crossing will appeal to many young readers. As they read the book, readers may be able to see their own friendships reflected in the story. Young readers can also learn about World War II, how it affected the world, and what life was life in the U.S. during the time. Also, the theme of lying and its consequences will teach readers how lying is frowned upon and how it affects them and the people surrounding them.<br /><br />As a future classroom teacher, I can see Lily’s Crossing having an important role. Because it is a quality historical fiction story, Lily’s Crossing can be used in my classroom as a way for my young students to come to know the world. Frank Serafini and Lindsey Moses state, “ in addition to informational texts, students can come to know the world by reading about human experiences through historical fiction,” (Serafini and Moses (2014), 13). Through reading Lily’s Crossing, my students will be able to learn what life was like during wartime in the 1940s. As a class, we can make a Venn diagram comparing and contrasting how our life today is different than Lilly and Albert’s lives. </span>
  <a data-text-id="13696780618411097936" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2751560134" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

  <div class="left bodycol">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2751560134" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5114019369174885288">I debated the rating on this quite a bit. Finally, based on a comparison with other books I've recently rated a 2, I had to go with 1 star because this one was just so much worse. <br/><br/>First things first: Lily is a MAJOR brat. I couldn't get over how many awful character traits she had. I don't mind flawed characters, in fact I typically like them best, but the problem with Lily is she rarely seems to learn from her mistakes. Honestly, I would hate teaching this child. If I don't like the MC, I have </span>
  <span id="freeText5114019369174885288" style="display:none">I debated the rating on this quite a bit. Finally, based on a comparison with other books I've recently rated a 2, I had to go with 1 star because this one was just so much worse. <br /><br />First things first: Lily is a MAJOR brat. I couldn't get over how many awful character traits she had. I don't mind flawed characters, in fact I typically like them best, but the problem with Lily is she rarely seems to learn from her mistakes. Honestly, I would hate teaching this child. If I don't like the MC, I have a really hard time liking a book. <br /><br />Secondly, the story was boring as all get out. There wasn't much of a plot that I could see. I liked the fact that the author tried to focus on a more unique part of WWII, instead of just kids escaping the Nazis, but I guess we know why author's use that plot - it's actually interesting. Lily meets Albert who escaped from the Nazis. He wants to swim back to Europe and Lily lies and says she can do that. (I'm majorly majorly summarizing here, there is some nuance to the plot, but that's the bones of it.) I'm sorry, but this was not exciting. <br /><br />The audio didn't help because of this weird music it would add in at random parts. I know they were trying to enhance the listening experience but it was jolting and irritating instead. The narrator herself was fine. <br /><br />I recently read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/828084.Pictures_of_Hollis_Woods" title="Pictures of Hollis Woods by Patricia Reilly Giff" rel="nofollow noopener">Pictures of Hollis Woods</a> which is also by Giff, it was MUCH better than this book and also won a Newberry Honor. I would definitely pick that one over this one. </span>

I will definitely use this book when I do historical fiction book clubs with my students. </span>

<div id="review_2347743522" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2347743522" />
    <a title="Darlene Foster" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2916220-darlene-foster"><img alt="Darlene Foster" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1582559024p2/2916220.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2347743522?book_show_action=true">Apr 09, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Darlene Foster" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Darlene Foster" href="/user/show/2916220-darlene-foster">Darlene Foster</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2347743522" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1798333651995076692">This is a wonderful story set in the mid-40s just towards the end of World War II. Lily is a young girl with a huge imagination and a bad habit of lying. Her mother died when she was little and she is being raised by her father and her grandmother. For a girl in America, the war seems far away and doesn't affect her until her father joins the army and is shipped overseas. When she meets Albert, a refugee from Hungary, she learns first hand how war can affect a family. I love how the author creat</span>
  <span id="freeText1798333651995076692" style="display:none">This is a wonderful story set in the mid-40s just towards the end of World War II. Lily is a young girl with a huge imagination and a bad habit of lying. Her mother died when she was little and she is being raised by her father and her grandmother. For a girl in America, the war seems far away and doesn't affect her until her father joins the army and is shipped overseas. When she meets Albert, a refugee from Hungary, she learns first hand how war can affect a family. I love how the author created a very real girl in Lily, who in spite of her faults, has a good heart. The descriptions of a time long ago are excellent and the story of family and friendship is still relevant today. </span>
  <a data-text-id="1798333651995076692" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2741808833" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2741808833" />
    <a title="Megan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1073025-megan"><img alt="Megan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1242312991p2/1073025.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2741808833?book_show_action=true">Mar 15, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Megan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Megan" href="/user/show/1073025-megan">Megan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1073025-megan?shelf=young-adult-childrens">young-adult-childrens</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1073025-megan?shelf=world-war-ii">world-war-ii</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1073025-megan?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1073025-megan?shelf=read-2019">read-2019</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2741808833" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17017535722321204129">In the summer of 1944, nothing goes as planned for Lily. She is supposed to spend the summer in Rockaway with her friend Margret and her father is supposed to visit every weekend, but her father must go overseas, and Margret’s family moves so that her father can find work. Lily is certain this will be the worst summer ever, until she meets a young boy named Albert who has also been affected by the war. Lily and Albert both tell lies, but their lies are generally harmless until one of Lily’s lies</span>
  <span id="freeText17017535722321204129" style="display:none">In the summer of 1944, nothing goes as planned for Lily. She is supposed to spend the summer in Rockaway with her friend Margret and her father is supposed to visit every weekend, but her father must go overseas, and Margret’s family moves so that her father can find work. Lily is certain this will be the worst summer ever, until she meets a young boy named Albert who has also been affected by the war. Lily and Albert both tell lies, but their lies are generally harmless until one of Lily’s lies puts Albert’s life in jeopardy. <br /><br />Eleven-year-old Lily is a naughty girl who lies, steals, sneaks into movies, and is generally mean to her grandmother. These aspects make her an unlikable protagonist although her flaws seem to be a result of her circumstances and she does change her behavior. Much of the plot surrounds Lily’s naughtiness and lies. The plot focuses on how World War II affected the lives of children in the United States. <br /><br />Lily’s Crossing has themes of loss, grief, friendship, and war. The setting of Rockaway is key to the story as Lily teaches Albert to swim and he dreams to swimming back to Europe to find his sister. Lily spends her days running rampant in Rockaway and defying her grandmother. <br /><br />My favorite part of the book is the letters Lily receives from her father abroad. In these letters he uses book titles to communicate with Lily, “He’s been trying to tell me all these weeks. Madeline and The Three Musketeers. Roland, the French Hero. All in France”<br /><br />In the backmatter, Patricia Reilly Giff states, “I remember the summer of 1944, remember the invasion and the news of the allied armies as they marched across France and liberated Paris late that August. I remember the fears of that times, and how personal it all was. I was surprised that other people, sometimes even adults, thought about the same things I did and had much the same worries. But most of all, I remember that friendship, in the secret world of childhood, added comfort and joy and was the very texture of my life.”<br /><br />There are loads of historical fiction books about WWII available for all ages. Lily’s Crossing offers a brief glimpse into this period from an American child’s perspective. Lily doesn’t really experience many of the harsh realities of war. I would classify Lily’s Crossing as being more about friendship than being about WWII. </span>
  <a data-text-id="17017535722321204129" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2378195913" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16048664308950128214">I like WWII stories. Really, I do. This book was weird. It had virtually no plot whatsoever beyond Lily wanted her father back. She rarely listened and did what she was told. Then when she did it, it was half-assed at best. She seemed angry when she had to do certain things. The basic premise was difficult to figure out. I think it was supposed to be how one little girl dealt with the war at home. She just struck me as a very spoiled girl who wasn't used to not having her way. The author remarks</span>
  <span id="freeText16048664308950128214" style="display:none">I like WWII stories. Really, I do. This book was weird. It had virtually no plot whatsoever beyond Lily wanted her father back. She rarely listened and did what she was told. Then when she did it, it was half-assed at best. She seemed angry when she had to do certain things. The basic premise was difficult to figure out. I think it was supposed to be how one little girl dealt with the war at home. She just struck me as a very spoiled girl who wasn't used to not having her way. The author remarks that she based it on her life. I feel bad for her. Partly that she had to go through that (my own grandma was only 3 in 1944) and partly because I hope she is not as bad as Lily was in the book. 3/5, unlikely to read it again. </span>
  <a data-text-id="16048664308950128214" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_969016585" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/969016585" />
    <a title="Audrey" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5436039-audrey"><img alt="Audrey" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1397520421p2/5436039.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/969016585?book_show_action=true">Jun 16, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Audrey" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Audrey" href="/user/show/5436039-audrey">Audrey</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5436039-audrey?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5436039-audrey?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5436039-audrey?shelf=1940s">1940s</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5436039-audrey?shelf=wwii">wwii</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5436039-audrey?shelf=juvenile">juvenile</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5436039-audrey?shelf=listens">listens</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer969016585&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer969016585" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16405024493492601422">This is an okay book, although Lily is a bit of a brat. I'm not really sure why it's a Newbery winner, though. I actually like <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/195644509?book_show_action=false' rel='nofollow noopener'>Willow Run</a> better, which is sort of a companion book about Lily's friend, Meggie. <i>Willow Run</i> was written several years after this book, though, and it seemed like a few things might have contradicted each other. But it was minor stuff (like when Meggie first saw the airplane factory) and not really a big deal.<br/><br/>In many ways, this actually has some similarities to <i>Willow Ru</i></span>
  <span id="freeText16405024493492601422" style="display:none">This is an okay book, although Lily is a bit of a brat. I'm not really sure why it's a Newbery winner, though. I actually like <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/195644509?book_show_action=false" rel="nofollow noopener">Willow Run</a> better, which is sort of a companion book about Lily's friend, Meggie. <i>Willow Run</i> was written several years after this book, though, and it seemed like a few things might have contradicted each other. But it was minor stuff (like when Meggie first saw the airplane factory) and not really a big deal.<br /><br />In many ways, this actually has some similarities to <i>Willow Run</i>. Both deal with overcoming a vice (stealing or thieving, respectively), grandchildren relating to their grandparents, the movies, a radio show, the loss and tragedy of war, and making friends. (I guess the first two are the main similarities.) Like <i>Willow Run</i>, this book also has some Catholic references—again, very naturally incorporated into the story. They go to Mass and Lily goes to a Catholic schools. There are mentions of a few stereotypically cranky nuns, but there's also a nice nun who is very encouraging of Lily's talent as a writer. (These mentions just caught my attention since I am Catholic.)<br /><br />Lily is a pretty mischievous kid, and I didn't find her very endearing. I also thought that she could've shown a bit more character growth, but perhaps it's more realistic that she didn't? Since this book is geared toward kids, hopefully they will pick up on the parts of her character <i>not</i> to emulate. She does swear a little when referring to her dreaded piano practice. It's just "damn," which doesn't bother me too much, but it's not a word I would want kids using. <br /><br /><u>Random Notes/Questions:</u><br /><br />I don’t think there was a movie from the 1940s called <i>Fair Stood the Wind for France</i> (at least not that I could find). It is a book, and they made a miniseries in the ‘80s, but there's nothing about a movie from the ‘40s. <br /><br />Why did Lily's dad just leave to join the war effort in 1944? Why not sooner? It also seems like he came home a little early. They act like the war is over after V-E Day, but there's still the Pacific theater. <br /><br />How’d Lily know not to let the cat stop moving? <br /><br />Albert doesn’t know what nuns are? <br /><br />Why didn't Albert write to his sister earlier?<br /><br />Some parts were very predictable (e.g., the violin, references to French books), but I guess this is a kids book. <br /><br />At the end of the book, if she’s writing to Albert, wouldn’t he say if he was going to be in Rockaway? <br /><br />I liked the author's note. It's neat that the setting was inspired by Giff’s own childhood memories of growing up on Rockaway Beach during the Second World War. I don't really get the title of this book, though. Where is Lily crossing to? Am I taking it too literally?<br /><br />2.5 to 3 stars. I didn't dislike this book; I just didn't love it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16405024493492601422" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer18145527321101574917">My major problem with this book is that I really couldn't understand why I was suppose to like Lily. She lies, sneaks in to moives, likes to accuse people of being Nazi (which can be dangerous), she is an indifferent student (except for books), eats candy with her friend that was suppose go to a soilder, and doesn't want to pratice the piano. Then again when I was 12 I never understood why I was suppose to like Harriet in Harriet the Spy. So right from the start it was hard for me to get into th</span>
  <span id="freeText18145527321101574917" style="display:none">My major problem with this book is that I really couldn't understand why I was suppose to like Lily. She lies, sneaks in to moives, likes to accuse people of being Nazi (which can be dangerous), she is an indifferent student (except for books), eats candy with her friend that was suppose go to a soilder, and doesn't want to pratice the piano. Then again when I was 12 I never understood why I was suppose to like Harriet in Harriet the Spy. So right from the start it was hard for me to get into this story. <br /><br />When I started I thought the book would be like Pictures of Hollis Wood which I remeber liking. Instead it turn out to slightly better than Eleven but, still not a great book for me. I finally had to start Roll of Thunder Hear My Cry.<br /><br />The major plot of the story is Lily's friendship with a boy named Albert. It was hard for me to get worked up about it because I really wasn't on Lily's side. It was okey but, nothing really special. Not to give anything away I thought Lily was a bit dense but, that could because Dewey was so smart in The Green Glass Sea.<br /><br />See CM Baggett's review.<br /><br />PS I almost forgot her friend Margaret shoplifts.<br /><br />PSS If you want a book about the Homefront during World War I would suggest Judy Blume's Starring Sally J. Freedman as Herself. Much better book and character.</span>

<div id="review_409913844" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/409913844" />
    <a title="Barb Terpstra" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2344070-barb-terpstra"><img alt="Barb Terpstra" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1333413711p2/2344070.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/409913844?book_show_action=true">Sep 08, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Barb Terpstra" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Barb Terpstra" href="/user/show/2344070-barb-terpstra">Barb Terpstra</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer409913844" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer211517631374578303">As I consider what I liked best about this story, I think it is the expression of Lily's contrary feelings. Remember when you were young and you loved your mom, but you disliked her too? When your mom showed you expressions of love, you may have shunned them. Contrary. A perfect expression of those teenage emotions. And stubborn. Too stubborn to give in to those soft feelings.<br/><br/>Lily has those feelings towards her Gram. She feels mad at her dad who is leaving her to serve in the war. She doesn't ha</span>
  <span id="freeText211517631374578303" style="display:none">As I consider what I liked best about this story, I think it is the expression of Lily's contrary feelings. Remember when you were young and you loved your mom, but you disliked her too? When your mom showed you expressions of love, you may have shunned them. Contrary. A perfect expression of those teenage emotions. And stubborn. Too stubborn to give in to those soft feelings.<br /><br />Lily has those feelings towards her Gram. She feels mad at her dad who is leaving her to serve in the war. She doesn't have a mom, she died long ago. Her best friend Margaret is leaving for the summer too. So Lily tells lies and stories to comfort herself. The only good thing is she is at her beloved home by the ocean in Rockaway. While there Lily has some adventures with a new friend, Albert, who has been orphaned by the war and has his own struggles. <br /><br />In essence, this story is about Lily's beginning to grow up. To understand that love and life is complicated. <br /><br />I really enjoy reading teen/young adult fiction. For one, you can read a story in an afternoon, and secondly, it's often better than much of the adult fiction that's out there.<br /><br />If you read aloud to your children, this would be a good option for your upper elementary student. If you just want a story to while away a few hours, this would fit the bill. </span>
  <a data-text-id="211517631374578303" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Darcy Stewart" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1852193-darcy-stewart"><img alt="Darcy Stewart" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/63520090?book_show_action=true">Jul 14, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Darcy Stewart" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Darcy Stewart" href="/user/show/1852193-darcy-stewart">Darcy Stewart</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer63520090" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer385589221458652660">In Lily's Crossing, Lily must move to Rockaway, NY for the summer. Her father is sent to Europe. Her father promises to tell her where he is secretly. Her best friend Margaret must move near a factory where her dad works. Albert a refugee from Hungary stays with the Orbans for the summer. Albert is looking for his sister Ruth who got sick in France and was taken a nunnery. Lily promises him that she will go with him to France to help find his sister. Over time Lily and Albert become best friends</span>
  <span id="freeText385589221458652660" style="display:none">In Lily's Crossing, Lily must move to Rockaway, NY for the summer. Her father is sent to Europe. Her father promises to tell her where he is secretly. Her best friend Margaret must move near a factory where her dad works. Albert a refugee from Hungary stays with the Orbans for the summer. Albert is looking for his sister Ruth who got sick in France and was taken a nunnery. Lily promises him that she will go with him to France to help find his sister. Over time Lily and Albert become best friends. At the end of the summer Albert returns to Canada. This is a wonderful book telling what the war was like living in the United States.</span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('my+5tpTt21ODccJSj59cvO4x6q/dp6xaxZBt4Xnnb6kATSGP2iGh1GGB81aHa7X7AIrU8LI9HlqIwI1VKP+IyQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('RZPdn3RNuNbNty4QKWPNRTnDuhPoh1ogxIQhOTC6xiDe8UWmOoHCUS9HHxQhlyQC13iETIcd6CCJ1MGNYaIhQA==')})

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer11435340013980003762">PATRICIA REILLY GIFF is the author of many beloved books for children, including the Kids of the Polk Street School books, the Friends and Amigos books, and the Polka Dot Private Eye books. Several of her novels for older readers have been chosen as ALA-ALSC Notable Books and ALA-YALSA Best Books for Young Adults. They include The Gift of the Pirate Queen; All the Way Home; Water Street; Nory Ryan</span>
  <span id="freeText11435340013980003762" style="display:none">PATRICIA REILLY GIFF is the author of many beloved books for children, including the Kids of the Polk Street School books, the Friends and Amigos books, and the Polka Dot Private Eye books. Several of her novels for older readers have been chosen as ALA-ALSC Notable Books and ALA-YALSA Best Books for Young Adults. They include The Gift of the Pirate Queen; All the Way Home; Water Street; Nory Ryan's Song, a Society of Children's Book Writers and Illustrators Golden Kite Honor Book for Fiction; and the Newbery Honor Books Lily's Crossing and Pictures of Hollis Woods. Lily's Crossing was also chosen as a Boston Globe-Horn Book Honor Book. Her most recent books are Number One Kid, Big Whopper, Flying Feet, Eleven, Wild Girl, and Storyteller. </span>
